<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_15773755">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15773755" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/921073-jonathan" class="left imgcol" title="Jonathan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452223659p2/921073.jpg" alt="Jonathan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15773755?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/921073-jonathan" class="user" title="Jonathan">Jonathan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780743278904" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who smell like patchouli</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jonathan by: </span>
      my birth certificate
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/921073-jonathan?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15773755">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16906611724146118084">Basically, you've got a seagull who just can't fit in with other seagulls. If this was written within the last decade, Jonathan would be coping with his outcast status by wearing a black trench coat and rolling 20-sided dice for fun. He would also achieve a loyal following of other socially awkward birds by totally kicking ass in Guitar Hero.<br /><br />Sadly, this was written in the halcyon days of the 70's, so Jonathan goes on a soul searching quest and learns how to fly better than any other seagull. Gra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16906611724146118084">Basically, you've got a seagull who just can't fit in with other seagulls. If this was written within the last decade, Jonathan would be coping with his outcast status by wearing a black trench coat and rolling 20-sided dice for fun. He would also achieve a loyal following of other socially awkward birds by totally kicking ass in Guitar Hero.<br /><br />Sadly, this was written in the halcyon days of the 70's, so Jonathan goes on a soul searching quest and learns how to fly better than any other seagull. Gradually, other seagulls join him and become awesome too.<br /><br />No, I'm not describing a children's picture book. I'm talking about a book that bookstores actually shelve in the "literature" section. I honestly think that there are more photographs of seagulls in this book than there are paragraphs. Anyway, some people call this book "inspirational", or "motivating." I'm guessing that these are the same people who consider accidentally getting two extra cheesesticks for free in their Papa John's order "a miraculous affirmation of a higher power."<br /><br />The only reason I gave this book two stars instead of one is that I was named after it. Honestly, who wants to be named after a shitty book? Think of the entire pantheon of literature. I could have been named Atticus Finch, or Heathcliff Earnshaw, or Beowulf. Instead I get Jonathan Livingston. Thanks a lot, Mom and Dad. No, really, you guys just sit back and relax, I'll roll this next doobie for you.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16906611724146118084">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1522392?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47436-mrelia" class="user" title="Mrelia">Mrelia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/47436-mrelia?shelf=stuffiwishihadntread" class="actionLinkLite">stuffiwishihadntread</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1522392">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16826764180219970240">I read this book after hearing for years that it was great and life-changing. I expected at worst that it wouldn't be quite as good as advertised. Boy was I in for a surprise!<br /><br />What I read was the biggest load of self-indulgent, pseudo-inspirational tripe I've read in my life!<br /><br />Apparently, the moral of the allegorical tale is that being "ordinary" is bad, ignoring practical needs to pursue your passion is good and if others don't understand you it's because you're a misunderstood genius/spiritually</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16826764180219970240">I read this book after hearing for years that it was great and life-changing. I expected at worst that it wouldn't be quite as good as advertised. Boy was I in for a surprise!<br /><br />What I read was the biggest load of self-indulgent, pseudo-inspirational tripe I've read in my life!<br /><br />Apparently, the moral of the allegorical tale is that being "ordinary" is bad, ignoring practical needs to pursue your passion is good and if others don't understand you it's because you're a misunderstood genius/spiritually superior being. <br /><br /><br />Maybe others don't understand you because you're always "borrowing" gas money, crashing on their couches and eating all their food. Ever think of that wasteoids? What's wrong with being a responsible member of society and pursuing spiritual enlightenment on your own dang couch?<br /><br /><br />Perhaps I take a dim view of this book's message because I've known too many people who "follow their dreams" and expect someone else to take care of their "mundane" needs.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16826764180219970240">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer692159133288899714">JLS isn't the freeloading bum who espouses following dreams and then gets wasted on your couch. He's the guy/gal who actually puts hard work, every da</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText692159133288899714">JLS isn't the freeloading bum who espouses following dreams and then gets wasted on your couch. He's the guy/gal who actually puts hard work, every day, into achieving his aspirations. He represents the dreamer who "does" and does it for the love of the doing. The moochers who spout off "follow your dreams", only to then get high, pass out on your couch, and accomplish nothing but putting you further into debt would be the masses of self-centered seagulls in the story. They're the bulk of the hippies in the 70's. JLS would be.. Steve Jobs. He was a hippy,yes. But he was hippy with a dream who put hard work into making that dream a reality. JLS is you. He's the good in all of us.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/963280-janet" class="left imgcol" title="Janet"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1384159276p2/963280.jpg" alt="Janet" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17323694?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 08, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/963280-janet" class="user" title="Janet">Janet</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780743278904" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who are inspired by Abraham Lincoln</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/963280-janet?shelf=life" class="actionLinkLite">life</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/963280-janet?shelf=spirituality" class="actionLinkLite">spirituality</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17323694">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7201918479624670400">"Most gulls don't bother to learn more than the simplest facts of flight--how to get from shore to food and back again," writes author Richard Bach in this allegory about a unique bird named Jonathan Livingston Seagull. "For most gulls it is not flying that matters, but eating. For this gull, though, it was not eating that mattered, but flight." <br /><br />Flight is indeed the metaphor that makes the story soar. Ultimately this is a fable about the importance of seeking a higher purpose in life, even if yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7201918479624670400">"Most gulls don't bother to learn more than the simplest facts of flight--how to get from shore to food and back again," writes author Richard Bach in this allegory about a unique bird named Jonathan Livingston Seagull. "For most gulls it is not flying that matters, but eating. For this gull, though, it was not eating that mattered, but flight." <br /><br />Flight is indeed the metaphor that makes the story soar. Ultimately this is a fable about the importance of seeking a higher purpose in life, even if your flock, tribe, or neighborhood finds your ambition threatening. (At one point our beloved gull is even banished from his flock.) By not compromising his higher vision, Jonathan gets the ultimate payoff: transcendence. Ultimately, he learns the meaning of love and kindness. <br /><br />I read this book when I was a teenager, it set the stage for a life of searching for a higher purpose and today, almost 40 years later, my life is heaven on earth. <br /><br />In Abraham Lincoln's words...<br /><br />"All my life I have tried to pluck a thistle and plant a flower wherever the flower would grow in thought and mind." Abraham Lincoln<br /><br />And M. Scott Peck's words...<br /><br />"Abandon the urge to simplify everything, to look for formulas and easy answers, and to begin to think multidimensionally, to glory in the mystery and paradoxes of life, not to be dismayed by the multitude of causes and consequences that are inherent in each experience -- to appreciate the fact that life is complex." M. Scott Peck </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7201918479624670400">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_337987724">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337987724" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="left imgcol" title="Jonathan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450116936p2/6313408.jpg" alt="Jonathan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/337987724?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 12, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="user" title="Jonathan">Jonathan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/386175.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780006490340" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=popularity-contest" class="actionLinkLite">popularity-contest</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=books-with-films" class="actionLinkLite">books-with-films</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer337987724">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2070671733019452451"><strong>The dismissive review of this text:</strong> What an absolute waist* of time! I mean OMG how bad is this!<br /><br /><strong>The intellectual review of this text:</strong> Well, um, I do believe that, um, this is positively remarkable. With only 87 pages Mr Bach produces a fable of such monumental importance to all humanity. He discusses the idea of alienation, provides a subtle sense of xenophobia and highlights the hamartia of humanity.<br /><br /><strong>The unsure student's review of this text:</strong> I think it was, like, sort of good. I mean I like the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2070671733019452451"><strong>The dismissive review of this text:</strong> What an absolute waist* of time! I mean OMG how bad is this!<br /><br /><strong>The intellectual review of this text:</strong> Well, um, I do believe that, um, this is positively remarkable. With only 87 pages Mr Bach produces a fable of such monumental importance to all humanity. He discusses the idea of alienation, provides a subtle sense of xenophobia and highlights the hamartia of humanity.<br /><br /><strong>The unsure student's review of this text:</strong> I think it was, like, sort of good. I mean I like the whole story of the seagull's learning to fly and all. I was sort of lost in seagull heaven that was not heaven and had no idea what was going on ya know?<br /><br /><strong>The working man's appealing to intellectual tendencies review:</strong> Well I think that the novella is top class. It has a fascinating story about birds, some great pictures (of birds) and well it really tells us something about how incredible we as people can be. We can make our own heaven as he says and we all don't have to be alienated.<br /><br /><strong>My review</strong>:<br /><br />Jonathan Livingstone Seagull and I may share a first name but that's about as far as we can be friends. He's an outsider in his flock and so I don't think that we can relate on a personal level. Although to be fair it's not his outsider tendencies and his rebellion against what seagulls should be doing that drives me away. No I'm perfectly fine with the fact that he wants to fly free and fast, fishing out at sea rather than scrabbling for chips and fish on quays and attending sporting matches at the Melbourne Cricket Ground. I don't think that I can approve of his extracurricular activities, however, which involve being transported to another plane of existence (because he can fly so well, no less) with strange spirit gulls. I mean my parents told me never to go off with total strangers and here Jonathan Livingstone Seagull does just that and ends up in another weird dimension which is heaven, but not heaven. After all, Jonathan, is told, heaven must be found inside us and we find it through perfection which is in in being. A little pretentious perhaps?<br /><br />What I dislike most about this fable is what I perceive as the intended message. I am completely opposed to the mystic new age idea of finding contentment and peace within oneself to find heaven. That is because I instead believe in there being a life after death which is not a movement up to new planes of existence as seen in this work but rather one final resting place which is eternal. Of course I must admit that the positive of this work was that it was short. Which made it easy to race through in half an hour.<br /><br />Read if you wish but I will not be classing this a must read classic. Nor will I ever attempt to read this again. Unless of course the fictional reviewers above chase me down and force me at gunpoint. Or if a dozen clowns tie me up with nylon cords and force me to choose between reading it or hearing Vogon poetry...<br /><br /><br />*the author of this review would like to inform that this is a poirposeful missspelling. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2070671733019452451">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13414879175619319093">Worth noting (if no-one mentioned it above) that the whole "The Kingdom is inside you" notion that gave rise to this "Heaven is found within" school o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13414879175619319093">Worth noting (if no-one mentioned it above) that the whole "The Kingdom is inside you" notion that gave rise to this "Heaven is found within" school of New Age philosophy comes from a classic mistranslation of the Greek in the New Testament. The actual Greek words mean "The Kingdom is already in existence among you" or "You are already in the midst of the Kingdom" and refers literally to the Kingdom as an EXTERNAL rather than INTERNAL thing.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_848277602">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/848277602" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="left imgcol" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1383845644p2/8734459.jpg" alt="Tadiana ? Night Owl?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/848277602?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="user" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?">Tadiana ? Night Owl?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=inspirational-and-religious-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">inspirational-and-religious-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=self-improvement" class="actionLinkLite">self-improvement</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=animalia" class="actionLinkLite">animalia</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=stole-from-dad" class="actionLinkLite">stole-from-dad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer848277602">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4546400886515727337">You know, sometimes you should just leave fond childhood memories alone.<br /><br /><img width="300" height="170" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504278.jpg" /><br /><br />But I have a hard time resisting any kind of (reading) challenge, so when Karly threw it down yesterday (see the thread to this review for her very funny and half-hearted trolling efforts), I felt compelled to go dig out my old copy of <em>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</em>--and it did take some digging--to see if I could justify my then-three-star review.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I can't.<br /><br /><img width="270" height="325" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504279._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />This flimsy and fluffy little book was a massive best-sell</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4546400886515727337">You know, sometimes you should just leave fond childhood memories alone.<br /><br /><img width="300" height="170" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504278.jpg" /><br /><br />But I have a hard time resisting any kind of (reading) challenge, so when Karly threw it down yesterday (see the thread to this review for her very funny and half-hearted trolling efforts), I felt compelled to go dig out my old copy of <em>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</em>--and it did take some digging--to see if I could justify my then-three-star review.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I can't.<br /><br /><img width="270" height="325" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504279._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />This flimsy and fluffy little book was a massive best-seller in 1972 and 1973. It's a VERY unsubtle parable about a seagull who decides that the mundane life of squawking and fighting for food is not for him. He wants to learn how to <strong>really</strong> fly.<br /><br /><img width="270" height="325" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504280._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />The other seagulls are not impressed with his stunts and aerial acrobatics.<br /><br /><img width="360" height="394" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422466947i/13504281.jpg" /><br /><br />But Jonathan Seagull is brave enough to defy the Flock and continue his search for perfection. <br /><br />It's all very inspiring and affirming and I can see why a lot of people still love it. There's actually a JLS website where people share their "seagull stories" of how they learned to overcome their doubts and fears and truly live, and they all tell each other how great they are. Fly free, beautiful white birds! And that's all fine, as long as you're not hurting innocent people in your search to Find Yourself (looking at you, mom in <em>How To Train Your Dragon 2</em>).<br /><br />But this book, as a piece of literature, has problems on so many levels: The heavy-handed symbolism. The simplistic worldview (spend all your time learning how to fly perfectly and all other problems will magically take care of themselves!).<br /><br />And the book tries to be all things to all people. Overcoming obstacles and achieving through your own determination and effort? Yup. Reincarnation? Got it. Christian symbolism? Covered. New Age mysticism? Don't get me started.<br /><br />2 stars, because even if it's on the simplistic and cheesy side, I still find a little inspiration and humor in the pages of this novella.<br />_________<br /><br />Earlier post: Karly tells me I'm way off base with my 3 stars here, which is based on my teenage reading of this book many, many moons ago. So I'm going to re-read this book (assuming I can find the dusty old copy that is hiding somewhere in my basement) and either agree with her or defend my position.<br /><br />It is on! *cracks knuckles*</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4546400886515727337">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer39145367">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer300252159082966686">ok, like I just wrote in a comment . . . this is probably one of those books that you have to read at a particular moment in your life. <br /><br />for me I was 15, had just run away from home and was in utter despair that the entire world was as mean, strict and narrow-minded as my peers seemed to be at that time. I longed for a friend, I longed for a sense of the world being more than what was drowning me. <br /><br />the friend who put this book in my hands also gave me Blind Melon's first album - and together these</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText300252159082966686">ok, like I just wrote in a comment . . . this is probably one of those books that you have to read at a particular moment in your life. <br /><br />for me I was 15, had just run away from home and was in utter despair that the entire world was as mean, strict and narrow-minded as my peers seemed to be at that time. I longed for a friend, I longed for a sense of the world being more than what was drowning me. <br /><br />the friend who put this book in my hands also gave me Blind Melon's first album - and together these two items may have literally saved my life. <br /><br />Bach's writing is simplistic, yes. it is almost childlike, yes. But there is for me an enduring wisdom to it. the seagull is obviously a very simplistic metaphor for a human, but in reality, particularly from where I was at the time, the idea of the "flock" just doing as it was told and spending all its time eating, shitting and talking about other gulls was not far off from my experience. <br /><br />as that 15 year old gypsy soul, I connected - not the gull - but with the sense that there had to be more to life and that the pursuit of perfection was not in vain. this book was like a child's story that assured me that my sense of things was not off-base. and I'm not kidding when I say that I felt that Jonathan Livingston Seagull was my first friend. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="300252159082966686">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1467512">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1467512" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely" class="left imgcol" title="J.G. Keely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1274333636p2/84023.jpg" alt="J.G. Keely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1467512?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/84023-j-g-keely" class="user" title="J.G. Keely">J.G. Keely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780743278904" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=philosophy" class="actionLinkLite">philosophy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/84023-j-g-keely?shelf=america" class="actionLinkLite">america</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1467512">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2645724796859561095">This book is a response to the flawed and disappointing underbelly of humanity, revealed for author Bach in Vietnam, the Kennedy assassination, the battles for Civil Rights and Feminism, and the Sexual Revolution. Unfortunately, it is not a work which embraces or explores those changes, but seeks an escape from the difficult questions of the world.<br /><br />Perhaps it should be unsurprising that the author would want to escape the everyday anxieties which mark the changing world. There is a sort of blind</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2645724796859561095">This book is a response to the flawed and disappointing underbelly of humanity, revealed for author Bach in Vietnam, the Kennedy assassination, the battles for Civil Rights and Feminism, and the Sexual Revolution. Unfortunately, it is not a work which embraces or explores those changes, but seeks an escape from the difficult questions of the world.<br /><br />Perhaps it should be unsurprising that the author would want to escape the everyday anxieties which mark the changing world. There is a sort of blind optimism in Jonathan Livingston Seagull, the sort you get when you take ancient and complex philosophy and distill it down into meaningless fluff. It is from this feel-good denial that the whole New Age movement springs, giving hope without guidance, and adding self-help to our self loathing.<br /><br />The surface of the water seems calm and glassy from afar. The ripples almost insensible. It is tempting to hope that the whirling eddies of hate, the tumult of inequality, and the maelstroms of fear do not persist beneath it. We shall someday find, when we must navigate Scylla and Charybdis, whether we have melted down our statues and our cannons both to build a monument to the lost.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2645724796859561095">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4733502">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13884680786943297733">I'm a sucker for this book. Throughout early Christianity, and especially in the second and third centuries, it was commonly believed that Jesus was just a really exceptional guy that God "adopted" and put to use as a redeemer of sins. Even after the Mark and Q Gospels were written and the circumstances of Jesus's birth were decided, the vote at Nicea was pretty slim that made Jesus the only begotten of the Father. Well, here's a book that goes back to the roots; any gull with a mind of his own</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13884680786943297733">I'm a sucker for this book. Throughout early Christianity, and especially in the second and third centuries, it was commonly believed that Jesus was just a really exceptional guy that God "adopted" and put to use as a redeemer of sins. Even after the Mark and Q Gospels were written and the circumstances of Jesus's birth were decided, the vote at Nicea was pretty slim that made Jesus the only begotten of the Father. Well, here's a book that goes back to the roots; any gull with a mind of his own can become the Son of God. I like that moral. And there's a chinese sage, so that's a plus too.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_102977693">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102977693" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1199525-cecily" class="left imgcol" title="Cecily"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1343028343p2/1199525.jpg" alt="Cecily" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/102977693?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1199525-cecily" class="user" title="Cecily">Cecily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780743278904" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=overrated" class="actionLinkLite">overrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer102977693">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14472508956969083448">This reminds me of Paulo Coelho's The Alchemist (the only one of his I've read). It's self-consciously "beautiful" and spiritual, but doesn't really have much depth. I enjoyed it in my late teens, when I had delusions of profundity, but I don't think it has much to impart to adults.<br /><br />It has 2* for nostalgia. If I read it now, I expect I'd only give it 1*.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_38898320">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38898320" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1713485-janice" class="left imgcol" title="Janice"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1237183907p2/1713485.jpg" alt="Janice" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38898320?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 05, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1713485-janice" class="user" title="Janice">Janice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone wanting to see further by flying higher</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Janice by: </span>
      The Love of My Life
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1713485-janice?shelf=religion" class="actionLinkLite">religion</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38898320">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9130525458190078402">Ethan just finished reading this book to the kids, and I had to update my rating from a three to a four. I guess this book just meant more to me right now than it did when I read it in the past. And I think the fact that it is one of Ethan's favorite books and he read it with so much adoration kind of helped it to grow on me. I feel like there is so much going on in both our lives that is exciting, but that personally I have become a little stagnant with where I am going. It is like I have becom</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9130525458190078402">Ethan just finished reading this book to the kids, and I had to update my rating from a three to a four. I guess this book just meant more to me right now than it did when I read it in the past. And I think the fact that it is one of Ethan's favorite books and he read it with so much adoration kind of helped it to grow on me. I feel like there is so much going on in both our lives that is exciting, but that personally I have become a little stagnant with where I am going. It is like I have become a regular gull and I am just trying to survive and find something to eat rather than learning how to fly. There was this one line that really touched me and I haven't been able to get it out of my head. Jonathon asks an elder seagull, “Is there no such place as heaven?" "No, Jonathon, there is no such place. Heaven is not a place, and it is not a time. Heaven is being perfect...You will begin to touch heaven, Jonathon, in the moment that you touch perfect speed...Perfect speed, my son, is being there." It has really made me think about how much of what I do every day I am not really there for. I have gotten into a rut of going through a lot of motions that I do not really experience or enjoy. So one of my resolutions for this coming year is to experience perfect speed, to be there for every moment of my life and the life we are creating for our family. And for the inspiration to do that, I definitely give this short little book four stars. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9130525458190078402">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1332125089880969529">Ode to the Paper Book: Holding a paper book in yours hands,smelling it ,feeling the pages as you flip them.Touching the cover.Looking back as you pass the bookshelf at an old friend.No, a computer can never replace that!A machine, cold ,impersonal,dead!As long as there are people in this crazy world of ours , the paper book shall survive!-Jonathan Livingston Seagull is a different kind of bird.He would rather fly as high as possible,than catch a fish.Recklessly diving,for fun, he cheats death ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1332125089880969529">Ode to the Paper Book: Holding a paper book in yours hands,smelling it ,feeling the pages as you flip them.Touching the cover.Looking back as you pass the bookshelf at an old friend.No, a computer can never replace that!A machine, cold ,impersonal,dead!As long as there are people in this crazy world of ours , the paper book shall survive!-Jonathan Livingston Seagull is a different kind of bird.He would rather fly as high as possible,than catch a fish.Recklessly diving,for fun, he cheats death many times.Of course Jonathan is an outcast who the others shun.Taught by an elder seagull about spiritualism(bird style),J.L.S. reaches gull heaven soon after(no he doesn't die). The seagulls big activity in paradise is to sit on a cliff, contemplating their navels, or wings or something like that(might sound a little strange to humans?).Bored, he begins teaching others. His followers begin calling Jonathan ,Son of the Great Gull, who else? Will he return to his flock back on Earth?And spread,not his wings, but the word? </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_466250808">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466250808" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6851560-fewlas" class="left imgcol" title="Fewlas"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395813645p2/6851560.jpg" alt="Fewlas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/466250808?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6851560-fewlas" class="user" title="Fewlas">Fewlas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/275984.Il_gabbiano_Jonathan_Livingston" title="Paperback 9788817131629" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer466250808">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6327375225922140257">Irritante e pericoloso. Una favola morale che vorrebbe insegnarci che la nostra volontà non ha limiti, che inseguire i nostri sogni dovrebbe essere la nostra unica preoccupazione. Ma: spronare al miglioramento è una cosa, istigare alla perfezione è un’altra.<br /><br />Che questo gabbiano voglia volare per il gusto di farlo e non solo per sopravvivere è cosa buona. Cosa altrettanto buona sarebbe voler insegnare anche che l’umana nostra vita enormi limiti ha, e che imparare a riconoscerli è una cosa buonissi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6327375225922140257">Irritante e pericoloso. Una favola morale che vorrebbe insegnarci che la nostra volontà non ha limiti, che inseguire i nostri sogni dovrebbe essere la nostra unica preoccupazione. Ma: spronare al miglioramento è una cosa, istigare alla perfezione è un’altra.<br /><br />Che questo gabbiano voglia volare per il gusto di farlo e non solo per sopravvivere è cosa buona. Cosa altrettanto buona sarebbe voler insegnare anche che l’umana nostra vita enormi limiti ha, e che imparare a riconoscerli è una cosa buonissima, sana, indispensabile. Usando una metafora gabbianesca: si vola anche per procacciarsi il cibo, non solo per diventare lo Usain Bolt dell’Olimpo gabbianesco. E, cosa ancor più deprimente ma vera: non tutti sono fatti di eteree piume, non tutti hanno le capacità necessarie per diventare figli di dio talentuosi superuomini; ebbene sì, c’è anche chi, per quanto si sforzi, non riesca a volare.<br /><br />Il termine “eugenetica” si è affacciato alla mia mente molto di più leggendo questo libriccino che quando lessi Galton. E non sto esagerando. <br /><br />Altro motivo di profonda irritazione è stato il fatto che, sebbene il tono generale sia quello dell’affabulatore pedagogo per bambini, Bach ci infila in mezzo (una riga sì e l’altra pure) termini che sinceramente, non essendo un’esperta di aerodinamica dei voli acrobatici, mi sono risultati alquanto difficili da comprendere; sicché questa volontà di indottrinare il genere umano con la pericolosa filosofia che tutto si può e che l’essere ordinari sia qualcosa di aberrante, viene inficiata dall’uso di un vocabolario che non tutti hanno la livingstoniana capacità di comprendere.<br /><br />Essere ordinari e riconoscere i propri limiti non è cosa aberrante. La cosa davvero aberrante è divulgare idee quasi naziste sotto la mentita spoglia di favole morali.<br /><br />Inoltre, sebbene io non venga bene in foto e non sia capace di fotografare, credo di avere un occhio buono abbastanza per dire che le fotografie inserite in questo libro non arrivano neanche alla mediocrità. <br /><br />Bocciato in toto. Il libro più irritante che io abbia mai letto. E pericoloso.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6327375225922140257">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="xhr_comment_photo">
    	<a href="/user/show/33349823-martyspringsteen98" alt="Martyspringsteen98"><img alt="33349823" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439282900p1/33349823.jpg" /></a>
  </div>
  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a href="/user/show/33349823-martyspringsteen98" style="font-weight:bold">Martyspringsteen98</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer4494838886163617672">Va bene che il libro possa non esserti piaciuto, ma da qua a definirlo "pericoloso" direi che ce ne vuole! Sinceramente non capisco perché ti dia così</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4494838886163617672">Va bene che il libro possa non esserti piaciuto, ma da qua a definirlo "pericoloso" direi che ce ne vuole! Sinceramente non capisco perché ti dia così fastidio il fatto che l'uomo, nel libro espresso con la metafora del gabbiano, possa rompere le catene che lo legano alla vita di tutti i giorni per sfruttare al meglio le proprie capacità. Nessuno ci impone di diventare l'Usain Bolt del nostro campo di applicazione ma non per questo non si può provare a perfezionare la propria tecnica e ad affinare il proprio ingegno. Personalmente apprezzo molto Richard Bach e, si, in alcuni passaggi risulta un po' arrogante, ma non trovo davvero alcun appiglio che possa ricollegare l'autore ad un'ideologia deviata come quella nazista, pertanto credo che quella tua frase sia frutto puramente di un'uscita infelice. Per quanto riguarda il vocabolario posso dirti che ho letto il libro a mio cugino di 6 anni e lui non ha avuto problemi a seguire la storia anche perché non mi sembra ci siano tutti questi termini così elevati. Certo, qualche accenno al volo viene fatto, ma in fondo l'autore era pilota...di cosa ti aspettavi potessero parlare i suoi libri? E comunque non bisogna essere aviatori per capire cosa sia una virata, o una corrente ascensionale.Detto questo spero che rivaluterai la tua opinione circa questo libro e Bach in generale perché non sai davvero cosa ti perdi ;)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4494838886163617672">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14406958141364979668">Condivido con MartySpringsteen, per quando riguarda la fotografia poi (te lo dico da appassionata) non esistono foto mediocri o meno, una foto deve co</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14406958141364979668">Condivido con MartySpringsteen, per quando riguarda la fotografia poi (te lo dico da appassionata) non esistono foto mediocri o meno, una foto deve comunicare qualcosa, e può anche farlo se la nitidezza o la luminosità non sono perfette. Inoltre, nonostante non sappia con precisione a quando risalgano quegli scatti, bisogna mettere in conto che all'epoca non esistevano ancora i teleobiettivi usati dai fotografi di National Geographic.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26273530" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1285606-michael" class="left imgcol" title="Michael"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1214851661p2/1285606.jpg" alt="Michael" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26273530?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 04, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1285606-michael" class="user" title="Michael">Michael</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71726.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title=" 9780380007790" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">dreamy teenagers or anyone else who wonders a lot</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1285606-michael?shelf=novels" class="actionLinkLite">novels</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1285606-michael?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1285606-michael?shelf=philosophy" class="actionLinkLite">philosophy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26273530">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7716180071075778425">I read this originally when I was about 11 years old I think. I had never read anything like it.<br /><br />I enjoyed the simplicity, and I think I identified with Jonathan more than a little—even at 11. <br /><br />As I think about this book almost 30 years later, I wish that I hadn't sold my copy of it, as I have an urge to re-read it and refresh my memory of Jonathan's struggles to break through. <br /><br /><br />July 2, 2009:<br /><br />Just re-read this for the first time in many years. "Let's begin with level flight." So much truth in that s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7716180071075778425">I read this originally when I was about 11 years old I think. I had never read anything like it.<br /><br />I enjoyed the simplicity, and I think I identified with Jonathan more than a little—even at 11. <br /><br />As I think about this book almost 30 years later, I wish that I hadn't sold my copy of it, as I have an urge to re-read it and refresh my memory of Jonathan's struggles to break through. <br /><br /><br />July 2, 2009:<br /><br />Just re-read this for the first time in many years. "Let's begin with level flight." So much truth in that simple statement.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7716180071075778425">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer387701735">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4820324661128986697">I read this when I was a kid just because it was lying around the house and it was a short, easy read. You couldn't escape it; its ubiquity was appalling. If you were alive in the 1970s you were basically issued it. It would come in a little bag with the Sunday paper like samples of breakfast cereal. <br /><br />I don't remember much about it. Something about a seagull, and I think he flies to the moon, which is stupid because duh, no air.</span>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1896527417583541979">Ha! How weird -- I was thinking about this book just yesterday and how I hadn't yet "rated" it on this site, then realized that I barely remember anything about it either. Something allegorical about a seagull trying to attain spiritual transcendence ... maybe. <br /><br />I think I hated it when I read it in high school (which wasn't long ago, but feels like it), yet who's to say if this was due to my underdeveloped literary skills at the time or to the actual quality of the book? Not sure I want to reread to find out ... it strikes me as some trendy pop-philosophy curio (<em>The Alchemist</em> of the '70s?) that wouldn't hold much meaning for an educated adult without the aid of a bong.</span>

        rated it

      Mum
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/1612410-sheree?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37599114">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12078091544879628760">A timeless inspirational story (published in 1970) about Johnathan Livingston Seagull, a seagull bored with the limitations of 'seagull life'. What sets this book apart is its simplicity in conveying thoughts on life and what the reader takes away depends on their personal perception. Motivation to seek a higher purpose, follow your dreams and not be held back by conventional limitations. </span>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15128466716777740626">Hi Jessica, it took me about 20 mins to read, it is only 93 pages and probably half of those are pictures, so a very quick read. I was about 13 when I read it first and I remember it being an ok story about a 'cool' seagull who didn't fit the norm. I certainly got a bit more out of it at 40yrs. I was unpacking boxes of old books and feeling a bit down, reading this little book again gave me a bit of lift. I really appreciated the story this time around whether I agreed with the spiritual aspects or not. So yes pick it up, it is such a quick read you will really have lost nothing if you don't enjoy it this time. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16114967907768409973">Where do I begin? The positives? It has a good, albeit somewhat patronizing message about thinking outside the box and reaching for your dreams. Also, it was very short. There. That said, I must say that I just don't get the hype. I found the story simplistic and uninspiring- just a bunch of 70's, new-age psycho-babble... and don't even get me started on the Neil Diamond movie (pretty pictures... that's all it was). AARRRGGGHHH! Fingernails on the chalkboard. I wish I liked it more as a good friend gave it to me with the tag that it was his favourite book and changed his life. Hmmmm... come to think of it, he was sort of a freak too...</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2574452813342648494">When I was in my first college year, a Spanish professor gave us the Spanish translation of this book, Juan Salvador Gaviota, to read. I found it to be a piece of rubbish. Pure selfhelp codswallop. When the same professor gave us the next book, Paulo Coehlo's Veronika Decides to Die, I complained at the Department and questioned her credentials. She was fired soon thereafter. <br /><br />If you need an author to give you his formula on how to live your own life, then this book is absolutely a must. If you want, however, to read true literature, then don't waste your time with this rubbish. It's codswallop, honestly. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/71728.Jonathan_Livingston_Seagull" title="Paperback 9780743278904" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">a few</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Viraj by: </span>
      Swanand

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1171789-viraj?shelf=god-religion-etc" class="actionLinkLite">god-religion-etc</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer22525866">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11407139438369660054">I was told that everyone who reads this book, find something different in it and it is an eye opener and what not. I found nothing great in this book. It is a simple story which could be an analogy at best. Look in old Marathi or other language literature for good analogies which are better eye openers or help thought process... <br /><br />Here is what I wrote immediately after reading the book. <br />The best thing about this book is that it gets over quickly as it is pretty small and of the 127 pages, about 27</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11407139438369660054">I was told that everyone who reads this book, find something different in it and it is an eye opener and what not. I found nothing great in this book. It is a simple story which could be an analogy at best. Look in old Marathi or other language literature for good analogies which are better eye openers or help thought process... <br /><br />Here is what I wrote immediately after reading the book. <br />The best thing about this book is that it gets over quickly as it is pretty small and of the 127 pages, about 27 are blank pages with the pictures of flying seagulls. Supposedly, from this book many people learned / interpreted different things. However, I found nothing great. If one really likes analogies (daakhale) one may read Dnyaaneshwar or Tukaaraam etc Sant folks. <br />Some messages I interpreted: <br />If one has to risk everything for a passion and to do something different from all others, one should. <br />No matter how much you get adept at a thing, you can still improve / improvise / learn more. <br />Once you know a lot of things, one should(?) go back to the same folks who left one earlier to help. <br /><br />Directly from the book (my comments in brackets): <br /><br />Pg.	Quoted<br />30	If we lift ourselves out of ignorance, we can find ourselves as creatures of excellence and skill. We can be free! <br />41	Boredom, fear, and anger causes one’s life to be short, and with those gone from one’s thought, one can live a long fine life indeed. <br />86	The gull sees farthest who flies highest. <br />87	If our friendship depends on things like space and tie, then when we finally overcome space and time, we have destroyed our own brotherhood. But overcome space, and all we have let is Here. Overcome time, and all we have left is Now. And in the middle of Here and Now, don’t you think that we might see each other more times? <br />125	Don’t believe what your eyes are telling you. All they show is limitation. Look with your understanding, find our what you already know, and you’ll see the way to fly. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11407139438369660054">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZJdf3DPQxnrtkI0ka5vONeqgOlLSw1PG5yoki235hV4BQ2APwQLSgGFI+Z8V+iiHo1f5S5seFGyNIyEZoWxzGw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

This&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText12469008847997236173\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Published by Rizzoli in 1975, Letter to a Child Never Born was quickly translated and sold in twenty-seven countries, becoming an extraordinary world success. It is the tragic monologue of a woman speaking with the child she carries in her womb. This letter confronts the burning theme of abortion, and the meaning of life, by asking difficult questions: Is it fair to impose life even if it means suffering? Would it be better not to be born at all?\nLetter to a Child Never Born touches on the real meaning of being a woman: the power to give life or not. When the book begins, the protagonist is upset after learning she is pregnant. She knows nothing about the child, except that this creature depends totally and uniquely on her own choices. The creation of another person directly within one’s own body is a very shocking thing. The sense of responsibility is huge; it is a heavy burden that gives life to endless reflections, from the origin of our existence to the shame of our selfishness. If the child could choose, would he prefer to be born, to grow up, and to suffer, or would he return to the joyful limbo from which he came? A woman’s freedom and individuality are also challenged by a newborn—should she renounce her freedom, her job, and her choice?     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16904.Richard_Bach">About Richard Bach</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/16904.Richard_Bach"><img alt="16904" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1420982726p2/16904.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1771877247817747045"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.com/Richard-Bach/e/B000AQ3C7C/ref=sr_ntt_srch_lnk_1?qid=1421247240&amp;sr=1-1"> <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356935.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="https://www.facebook.com/jlseagullcommunity"> <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356936.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/jls_community"> <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356937.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://instagram.com/jls_community"> <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356938.jpg" /></a> <br />Since <em>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</em> - which dominated the #1 spot on the New York Times Bestseller List for two consecutive years - Richard Bach has touched millions of people through his humor, wisdom and insight.<br /><br />With over 60 million copies of his books sold, Richard Bach remains one of the world's most beloved authors. A former USAF fighter pilot, Air Force captain and latter-day barnstorm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1771877247817747045"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://www.amazon.com/Richard-Bach/e/B000AQ3C7C/ref=sr_ntt_srch_lnk_1?qid=1421247240&amp;sr=1-1">
  <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356935.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="https://www.facebook.com/jlseagullcommunity">
  <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356936.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/jls_community">
  <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356937.jpg" /></a> <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://instagram.com/jls_community">
  <img width="45" height="45" class="escapedImg" alt="" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421306585i/13356938.jpg" /></a> <br />Since <em>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</em> - which dominated the #1 spot on the New York Times Bestseller List for two consecutive years - Richard Bach has touched millions of people through his humor, wisdom and insight.<br /><br />With over 60 million copies of his books sold, Richard Bach remains one of the world's most beloved authors. A former USAF fighter pilot, Air Force captain and latter-day barnstorming pilot, Bach continues to be an avid aviator-author, exploring and chronicling the joys and freedom of flying, reporting his findings to readers.<br /><br />His most recent works include <em>Travels with Puff</em>, which recounts Bach's journey from Florida to Washington state in his small seaplane, Puff, and <em>Illusions II: The Adventures of a Reluctant Student</em>, which incorporates Bach's real-life plane crash.<br /><br />In October 2014, the never-before-published Part Four to <em>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</em> was published.<br /><br />Readers can find more about Richard and his work at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.richardbach.com" target="_blank">www.richardbach.com</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1771877247817747045">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1743336-jonathan-livingston-seagull---a-story">Quotes from Jonathan Livingst...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
